Important News Two

Ministry of Finance's 18th Fiscal Year Financial Report (Continued) 69

However, although tariff revenue has increased, the repayment of principal and interest on foreign loans and war indemnities has also greatly increased due to the high price of gold and the low price of silver, almost offsetting each other. It is estimated that more than £8.5 million must be allocated from customs and salt taxes each year to repay these loans and indemnities. The following table lists the loan and indemnity repayments (calculated in national currency) and their conversion rates for recent years:

Year Gold Pound to National Currency Payout in National Currency

Rate (Approximate) (Approximate Number)

14th Year (Average) Each Pound converted to

National Currency 8.9 Yuan 760,000,000 Yuan

18th Year (Average) 11.7 Yuan 1,000,000,000 Yuan

19th Year (Average) 16.7 Yuan 1,420,000,000 Yuan

20th Year (Average) 21.6 Yuan 1,840,000,000 Yuan

In order to encourage domestic commerce, the government completely abolished re-import duties, half duties on subsidiary ports, and the five inland regular customs duties on January 1, 20th year. The five inland regular customs duties on imported foreign goods have also been abolished. As for the regular customs duties on local goods, they will also be abolished immediately after the export tariff rules are revised. The government has suffered huge losses after abolishing the above taxes, but it is willing to bear the pain for the sake of domestic commercial interests.

The first new tariff after the complete autonomy of customs duties was implemented on January 1, 20th year. The following principles were followed when drafting the new tariff: (1) The import tax on raw materials necessary for the development of domestic industry should be reduced. (2) The government should support domestic industries that need to be developed as much as possible to prevent them from being affected by foreign goods competition. (3) The increase or decrease in import tariff rates in the 19th year compared with the 18th year to compensate for the tax reductions are as follows:

Goods Percentage Increase Decrease

Imported Goods 10 percent Tax rate reduction

Same as above 43 percent Tax rate same as 18th year

Same as above 21 percent Increase of 2.5 percent

Same as above 9 percent Increase of 5 or 7.5 percent

Same as above 10 percent Ad valorem increase of 10 percent or more. The largest increase in tax rates is for matches and porcelain. Other items such as sugar, cement, glass, soap, cosmetics, silk, rayon, and woolen fabrics have also seen increases in tax rates compared to before. The high import tax rates in our country today are comparable to those of heavily taxed countries in Europe and America.

It is extremely difficult to predict income based on the new tariff rules. The income situation of the past three years is not sufficient to serve as a standard. Generally speaking, the global economic downturn will inevitably hinder commerce, and the low silver price will inevitably reduce import trade. At the same time, the increase in tariffs will also hinder import trade. In the future, tax evasion may become more frequent. To illustrate this, the import tax rate on silk fabrics was originally set at 7.5 percent in the 17th year, and increased to 22.5 percent in the 18th year. Afterwards, the annual import trade of silk fabrics actually dropped from Customs Tael 425,000 to 152,000. Looking at the domestic economic situation, I deeply feel that the import tax rate on ordinary imported goods cannot be increased again in the near future. The economic principle that higher tax rates lead to lower income is indeed true.

Salt Affairs Since the reorganization of the Salt Affairs Inspectorate in accordance with the new regulations, the authority to collect taxes and weigh and release salt in each region has been gradually restored in a unified manner. The authority of the Inspectorate on both sides of western Hubei has now been completely restored. Interference with the authority to collect taxes and weigh and release salt in the Fujian region has been completely prohibited. The duties of the Inspectorate in the Guangdong region had been suspended for many years, and branch offices in the region were established one after another in the 19th year, and have now achieved considerable results. Henan Province has never had an inspection agency, but the Henan Salt Affairs Tax Collection Bureau was established in November of the 18th year, but was only able to actually collect taxes in December of the 19th year due to the influence of the current situation. Now all salt affairs inspection branches in the country have been completely restored, and the Inspectorate's internal affairs have also been actively reorganized. There have been significant changes in the important officials in the office this year. During the spring and autumn seasons of the 19th year, transportation in several important salt regions was obstructed and transportation was suspended due to military influences. However, the salt tax revenue in the second half of the 19th year far exceeded the revenue in the same period of the 18th year. A comparison of the salt tax revenue for the two periods is listed below:

Revenue from July to December of the 18th year Revenue from July to December of the 19th year

July 8,905,943 Yuan 13,082,116 Yuan

August 8,739,908 Yuan 9,928,016 Yuan

September 12,145,726 Yuan 12,578,082 Yuan

October 11,156,885 Yuan 14,087,985 Yuan

November 9,267,794 Yuan 12,504,725 Yuan

December 7,204,700 Yuan 12,627,424 Yuan

Total 57,519,956 Yuan 74,808,298 Yuan

The total revenue of the Salt Affairs Inspectorate in the 18th fiscal year increased by more than 27 million yuan compared with the average annual revenue of the previous five years (from the 12th to the 16th year of the Republic of China).

In the 18th fiscal year, a total of £817,790 in British currency, equivalent to 10,818,113 yuan in national currency, was repaid from salt funds for various foreign debts. In the first half of the 19th fiscal year (from July to December of the 19th year), £654,351 in British currency was repaid for foreign debts, equivalent to 11,490,479 yuan in national currency.

In the spring of the 19th year, due to the daily decline in the price of silver, the amount of foreign debt to be paid by each region set in October of the 18th year was insufficient to cover the repayment of debts when they became due. Therefore, starting in April of the 19th year, all scheduled quotas were uniformly increased by 30 percent.

Although the price of gold soared this year and the funds to be paid by several regions in the north province were intercepted by the Shanxi side, all funds that should be paid and supplemented as stipulated in the Salt Affairs Loan Declaration in September of the 18th year were still allocated on schedule without delay.

Except for those affected by military affairs, the performance of the provinces and regions that implemented the various new systems promulgated in the 17th fiscal year for tobacco and alcohol taxes this year was even more remarkable. The tax rate for public sales of tobacco and alcohol in all provinces was uniformly set at 20 percent to show unification. Significant progress has also been made in abolishing local surcharges and miscellaneous levies. The registration methods for tobacco and alcohol merchants have been carried out in all provinces except for remote areas. The regulations on public sales of tobacco, the tax regulations on foreign wines, the tax regulations on various types of tobacco business licenses, and various inspection and fine regulations either still used the old system or the provinces governed themselves, and were unable to fully comply with the regulations. All of these were re-ordered and promulgated this year. For the convenience of implementation, although various tobacco and alcohol regulations were ordered by the Ministry, the detailed implementation rules and forms were all allowed to be drafted by the provincial bureaus after considering the local situation and submitted for verification and approved by the Ministry. The revenue from tobacco and alcohol taxes in all provinces has gradually increased since the previous year. The direct revenue of the national treasury was approximately 1.25 million yuan per month in the six months from July to December of the 19th year.

The greatest progress in stamp duties this year has been the promotion of stamp duties in concessions. In the past, Chinese merchants operating in leased territories often evaded affixing stamps. After active negotiations with the concession authorities, they have gradually complied. Now, the Shanghai Public Concession and the French Concession have successively established offices in Shanghai to handle all stamp duty matters. Once the source of taxation is promoted, income will also increase sharply.

The contractor system (where various groups purchased a fixed amount of stamps each year) was ordered to be abolished in the 17th fiscal year. This year, the work was continued and the actual posting of stamps was strictly enforced, resulting in satisfactory results. The contractor system was completely prohibited at the end of the 18th fiscal year. Significant progress has also been made this year in unifying stamp tax票. The new tickets manufactured by the Ministry are now being used and affixed throughout the country.

In addition to strictly enforcing new systems and selecting personnel to go to towns and cities for practical inspections, the Ministry also re-verified the expenses of various bureaus to increase revenue and reduce expenditure. As a result, the average monthly direct revenue of the national treasury in the five months from July to November of the 19th year reached 600,000 yuan. However, this increase in revenue is due to effective reorganization, peace, emphasis on the overall situation, and pacification. Cigarette Tax In April of the 19th year, the area for cigarette tax collection was expanded to Guangxi. In September, Henan also changed to unified tax collection. The method of collecting goods transported to Weihaiwei and Dalian was also improved this year. Since March of the 19th year, several provinces have successively experienced military events, resulting in a shortage of tax revenue. During the military period, the average monthly revenue was only 2.7 million yuan. After the end of the military events in October, tax revenue also increased accordingly, with monthly revenue of approximately 4 million yuan. (To be continued)

Minister of Communications of the League of Nations Arrives in Bengbu 70

Investigating the Huai River Situation

Bengbu Correspondence The Minister of Communications of the League of Nations, Haas, and the Minister of Economic Affairs, Souald, and the Minister of Health, Lakshman, have come to China one after another at the invitation of our government to study various issues in China. They will provide considerable assistance to various construction projects. Haas is particularly interested in our country's transportation and water conservancy projects. He has repeatedly investigated the progress of the projects with the competent authorities in Beijing. He also accompanied his engineering expert, Luke Xi (Luke is a traffic commissioner of the League of Nations), to the Huai River Guidance Committee to inquire in detail about the progress of the Huai River Guidance Project and the progress plan. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek specially asked him to take the opportunity to inspect the Huai River situation and contribute his findings to the Huai River Guidance Committee when he feasted Haas in Beijing. Jiu arrived in Bengbu on the night of the 12th and stayed at the Transportation Villa on Erma Road. They are scheduled to return to Bengbu in the afternoon, and then go east to Linhuai for inspection (16th).

Shantou Relieves Unemployed Overseas Chinese Returning to the Country 72

Shantou Correspondence Due to the decline in the price of rubber and tin ore in the Nanyang Islands, the government restricts production, so industry and commerce are depressed, and the number of unemployed overseas Chinese returning to the country is increasing day by day. Since last year, no less than several thousand people have been sent back to Shantou by the British and Dutch authorities. Wandering on the road, it is very pitiful. The fellow villagers associations in Shantou are unable to provide relief due to the continuous arrival of these overseas Chinese. They have appealed to the government on behalf of the victims. The provincial government then formed a Relief Committee for Unemployed Overseas Chinese last month, and the Construction Department issued a notice to the Chaozhou-Meizhou transportation agencies that overseas Chinese who are old, weak, or carrying children and who have an official letter with the seal of the Unemployment Relief Association will be exempt from boat and car fares so that they can return to their hometowns to reunite and not be displaced in the middle of the journey. Chen Weitao was then sent to Shantou to investigate everything and find ways to accommodate them, and allocated 10,000 yuan to Chen to set up an overseas Chinese reception center in Shantou to accommodate them. Chen arrived in Shantou on the Chaozhou wheel on the 10th and was preparing at the Overseas Chinese Mutual Aid Society. Mayor Zhang Lun of Shantou returned to his hometown of Dabu on the 9th to investigate the coal mines near Dama. It is said that the coal field is in Han.

Chaoyang Nanling Red Bandits Flee to Zijin 73

Shantou Correspondence The Erling Mountains, which border Chaoyang, Puning, and Huilai, stretch for more than a hundred miles. The remnants of the Red Army's 47th and 49th Regiments gather in the mountains and often harass the three counties of Chaozhou, Puning, and Huilai. Xiang Hanping of the 62nd Division once convened a conference of military and civilian officials from the three counties of Chaozhou, Puning, and Huilai in Shantou in mid-February to suppress bandits. It was decided to use the method of encirclement to build fortresses and watchtowers in Huilai Lin Zheshi, Chaoyang Lin Zhao Township, and Pu Kuan Wangtianshi, and install long-distance telephones for more than 500 miles around the mountain to prevent bandits from going out to loot and starve to death in the mountains. Wu Jianhong, Luo Jinying, and Luo Xiuli were assigned to garrison the key points of the three counties of Chaozhou, Puning, and Huilai to prevent the bandits from escaping. The Red Bandits in Nanling were panicked. On February 23, about 800 people, more than 200 short guns, and three mobile machine guns suddenly emerged from Nanling into Huilai. On the 24th, they fled through the Meitian area of Huilai and were intercepted by Liang Yanxiang of the 1st Battalion of the Luo Regiment. More than 100 bandits were killed on the spot, and the rest fled to the Beixi area of Lufeng County, where they were intercepted by the 2nd Battalion of the Luo Regiment, led by Song Yifen, and killed the pseudo-Red Army Regiment Commander Lin Junjie. Liang Ying heard that the battle had occurred in Beixi and set off from Kuitan, Huilai, on March 2 to pursue them. On the 5th, he assisted Song Ying and the Haifeng garrison to suppress the Red Bandits in Jieshixi. Seeing our army's arrival, they fled to Dashan, Paozi Village, Zijin County. Liang Ying and others returned to Lufeng City from Jieshi on the 7th. There has been a telegram to Shantou reporting that a group of Red Bandits have gathered in Nanling and are said to be fleeing elsewhere (March 10).

The Eastern Railway Bureau Tightens Meeting 75

Will Dismiss Chinese Workers for the Second Time

Harbin Correspondence Since the decline of the Eastern Railway's business last autumn, it has remained sluggish. Although the reasons for this are due to the depression of the northern Manchurian market, the gold-based freight rates are unsuitable for the silver-based business environment, and the Dongtie-Wutie agreements are lower than the Mantetsu, making it impossible for goods to be transported south. However, this is a planned and organized strategy of Soviet Russia, so it is not easy to change. On the 10th and 11th of this month, the Railway Bureau held a road affairs meeting attended by all the directors and engineers of the bureaus and departments, totaling more than one hundred people. On the first day, the Russian Bureau Director, Rudyi, gave a speech, saying that the responsibility of accountants is not only to keep accounts, but also to pay attention to the number of expenses not exceeding the fixed range. If the expenses exceed the fixed amount, they must report to the superiors to find a way to correct them. The travel time of freight cars must be the same as that of passenger cars in order to save time and transport more goods. The purchase of materials should be handled by the materials department to stipulate economical methods to avoid being uneconomical. At the end of the two-day meeting, dozens of measures were stipulated for the entire road to economize and increase revenue. All engineering and technical budgets should be based on the 1924 standards to achieve considerable results. At the closing meeting at 7:00 p.m. on the 11th, Mo Dehui and the Chinese and Russian directors attended. Mo delivered a speech, saying that the Eastern Railway is a transportation line between Europe and Asia, and is not only closely related to the transportation between China and the Soviet Union, but also occupies a place in world transportation. If it can be managed with daily progress and meritorious service, it will also be the glory of China and the Soviet Union. The business of the Eastern Railway depends on transportation. Since the two seasons last year, with the changes in the world economy and the sluggish sales of special products in northern Manchuria, business has plummeted. We should seek ways to relieve the situation. The current situation of the Eastern Railway lies in implementing austerity and financial management policies, in increasing revenue and reducing expenditure. Staff reduction and salary reduction are just one of the events. Other payments must be verified in everything. Everyone should embrace an austerity policy, and only by working together can we overcome this difficulty. On the afternoon of the 12th, the Russian Bureau Director of the Railway Bureau again hosted a banquet at the Railway Club for all the participants to discuss the implementation of the austerity plan. It is said that there may be a second batch of large layoffs this month, and the internal decision is to lay off 300 Chinese workers in 36 factory sheds. This matter has been proposed by the Russian Bureau Director to the Board of Directors, and the Chinese and Russian directors are still in negotiations and have not yet decided (12th).

Jiangsu Province Fisheries Protection Conference 77

The Jiangsu Province Coastal Fisheries Protection Conference held its opening ceremony in the provincial government conference room yesterday (16th). Thirty-two representatives from the Ministry of Industry, Finance, and Navy, various fisheries administrative agencies, and county fisheries associations attended. First, Chairman Ye Chucang of the provincial government reported that today's fisheries protection conference in the province brought together representatives from all fisheries-related agencies in the province and coastal defense agencies to jointly discuss the extremely long coastline of Jiangsu. The province is a prosperous province for fisheries. In recent years, on the one hand, it has been invaded by Japanese fishing boats and, on the other hand, it has been harassed by pirates. The future of the fishery has generally plummeted. Today, we will discuss protection methods based on the good opinions of the representatives. The province has not yet established complete fishery protection facilities, so the fishermen have not been able to get rid of the suffering they have suffered. The administrative agency is very sorry. Now, under the supervision of the representatives, we will discuss more effective methods without empty talk. The future of the province's fishery will have some hope. Then, the two department heads, Hu Puan and He Yushu, delivered speeches, saying that they were very grateful for everyone's enthusiastic participation. They hope that you can add a layer of protection to the lives of the fishermen who are crying out for help and that you believe that this meeting will have concrete measures. Then, Li Shixiang, a representative of the Ministry of Industry, and representatives of fishermen's organizations delivered speeches one after another, and then took pictures and dispersed. It is reported that the proposals will be reviewed in two groups today, the first being the fisheries group and the second being the protection group. The meeting was chaired by Ye Chucang in the morning and He Yushu in the afternoon. After the review meeting was completed, a dinner was held in the auditorium at 6:00 p.m.

Wuxi 81

Strict Pressure for Old Debts: The Department of Finance, considering the substantial arrears in land tax from counties of the 16th, 17th, and 18th classes, decided at a provincial government meeting to rigorously investigate and collect these debts to cover the budget deficit for the second half of the current year. A general order was issued to all counties, requiring them to separately list the owed land tax and debts owed by the people and setting a deadline for complete payment within a long or short timeframe this year. However, to date, few have reported payment by the deadline. Therefore, special commissioners are being dispatched to counties with larger arrears to urge payment and prevent delays. Cheng Jingchuan has been appointed as the commissioner for Wuxi, Wujin, and Jiangyin counties. Commissioner Cheng arrived in Wuxi yesterday and, together with Zhuang Yeguang, the director of the Finance Bureau, is meticulously investigating and collecting the land tax arrears and people's debts, setting a four-month deadline for complete recovery. A meeting is scheduled today to gather all tax collectors at the county office for instructions.

A Shocking Incident of Local Bandits Robbing and Injuring a Monk: In the 85th tu (a local administrative division) of Kaihua, 14th District, there is an ancient temple called Chishi Ridge Temple. The abbot, Monk Yueming, was known to possess some money. Xue Chunbao, a local from Shixiang Shang Village (originally a carpenter and currently the tu head), coveted this money. Xue Chunbao and others broke into the temple twice last year, causing significant losses. Yueming, unwilling to cause trouble, did not report the incidents to the county government. However, Xue Chunbao and his gang, believing the monk to be weak and easily bullied, led by Xue Chunbao, his son Quan Gen, and relatives Genfa, Genfu, Renfa, A Qiao, Long Sheng, Genpei, and more than ten others, armed with knives and clubs, scaled the wall and entered the monk's bedroom around 10 PM the night before. They dragged Yueming from his bed and attacked him with knives, causing severe throat injuries. Xue Chunbao and the gang then ransacked the temple, searching every box and chest for two hours, stealing 275 silver dollars and a mosquito net. Yesterday, Monk Yueming went to the city to report the incident to the County Court for an injury examination, submitting a list of the bandits and requesting an investigation by the Jiangsu Provincial Court. The Jiangsu Province Silkworm Seed Industry Association held its inaugural meeting yesterday morning at 10 AM at the Silk Factory Association. Attendees included Shao Shenpei from Dayou Silkworm Seed Farm, Wan Yuncheng from Zhenjiang Seed Production Farm, He Shangping from Nanjing Seed Production Farm, and over 80 representatives from various farms. Zhang Renjie, a representative from the County Party Consolidation Association, also attended to provide guidance. Shao Shenpei was elected as the temporary chairman, who reported the purpose of the meeting and discussed the regulations. The meeting continued at 2 PM, during which committee members were elected. As a result, 11 seed production farms, including Dayou, Zhenjiang, Guan, Sanwu Guan, Dachina, Li Wu, Yongtai, Hu Guan Cooperation Original Seed Farm, Yousheng, and Yonghe, were elected as executive committee members. Dayou, Zhenjiang, Sanwu Guan, Guan, and Yousheng were mutually elected as standing committee members. The Zhenjiang Seed Production Farm was elected as the chairman. The meeting was adjourned after the election of the committee members.

Changzhou 82

Abducted Student Escapes Danger: Xu Heshang, a student at the Qianhua Vocational School in Wuyi, recently returned to his hometown of Mapiqiao to recuperate from an illness. He was kidnapped by bandits on the 26th of last month. Xu's father, Bingwen, received a letter from the bandits demanding 8,000 yuan. He planned to raise 1,000 yuan first and send someone to negotiate. The Nan Tuan branch of Sanhekou near that location received a report on the 15th of this month that bandits frequently appeared in the Jiangjiaxiang area of Ningbei Township. The branch dispatched its patrol team, together with the chief and police of the second police station of the fifth sub-bureau, to surround and search Jiang Yaosheng's house. They apprehended Jiang Yaosheng while he was having lunch at home and rescued the hostage Xu Heshang from the house. They were brought to the Sanhekou Merchant Corps branch for preliminary interrogation. The interrogation revealed the names of several accomplices, and further searches were conducted. At Hengshan Anqiao, they encountered the bandit Wu Xinrong and others. As they prepared to pursue them, Wu fired a gun to resist arrest, injuring a farmer named Bao Jinfu in the right leg. The security team bravely stepped forward and captured Wu. On the afternoon of the 16th, the Merchant Corps branch handed over the captured bandits Jiang and Wu to the Merchant Corps headquarters in the city, who then transferred them to the county government for interrogation. Xu Heshang, who had become seriously ill in the bandits' den, was taken back by his father for medical treatment. Bao Jinfu, who was injured, was sent to the hospital for examination.

Scheduled Boat Robbed En Route at Shiqiao: A scheduled boat from Hengshan Bridge in Wuyi was robbed on the evening of the 15th. While traveling from the city towards the countryside at Yangtou Bridge, several armed bandits suddenly boarded the boat and robbed it. They stole nine pieces of silk purchased in the city by the Xietai Xiang foreign goods store, as well as silver dollars and other belongings from the passengers. After the incident, the boat owner, Xu Genghong, reported the case to the Fifth Public Security Sub-Bureau. Zhang Qingchun, the owner of the Xietai Xiang store, reported the significant loss of silk to the county government on the 16th, requesting the police to assist in the arrest of the bandits and the recovery of the stolen goods.

Changshu 83

Zhitang Again Suffers Robbery: On the afternoon of the 14th, around 7 PM, Zhitang Town in the Zhengxiu District was once again robbed. More than 20 bandits armed with Mauser pistols and other weapons arrived in the town and began robbing several households, including Liu F茂 Mao's rice store. Someone immediately rushed to the Zhitang jurisdictional Fifth Public Security Sub-Bureau to report the incident. Yang Zhenkun, the director of the sub-bureau, dispatched police to arrest the bandits, but they had already fled after the robbery. A total of 15 businesses, including rice stores and cloth stores, were robbed. As Director Yang and the police were about to return to the sub-bureau, they spotted a suspicious person. They approached and apprehended him, finding a Mauser pistol bullet and a shell casing on the ground next to him. They immediately sent a team to pursue the bandits and took the suspect to the sub-bureau for interrogation. The suspect identified himself as Yuan Baiwen from Yuelai Town, Haimen, and claimed he was heading to Chu Pu, intending to go to Ma Shan to find work. Director Yang, considering the case was related to the robbery, drew a map of the robbed locations and sent it, along with the suspect Yuan Baiwen, to the General Bureau on the 15th for further investigation by the county government.

Danyang 84

Compilation of Robberies in the Northeast Countryside: Around 3 AM on the 13th of this month, bandits, forty or more in number, suddenly surrounded Xizhuang Village near Lingkou and robbed every household. The villagers were awakened from their dreams. The young and strong climbed to the rooftops and sounded gongs. Neighbors who heard the alarm came to the rescue, but the bandits fired their guns and fled. Also, last night, more than 20 bandits suddenly came to the home of farmer Sheng Bingshou in Nanmazhuang Village, 5th District. They scaled the wall and entered the house. As they were searching, the village chief Lu Junxiang alerted the police and called for help. The villagers gathered, and the bandits, realizing they were outnumbered, fired their guns and fled.

Captured Fugitive Bandit: Ding Jisi, a resident of Xue Village, Zhenjiang, has a history of misbehavior and has repeatedly committed robbery and extortion. He was arrested this month by the Baozhen Public Security Sub-Bureau and temporarily detained at the bureau. Unexpectedly, the criminal escaped in the middle of the night and fled to Liuru Village in the southern countryside of the county. Villagers noticed him and captured him on the spot. He has now been handed over to the county government for interrogation.

Yangzhou 85

Disturbance Caused by Use of People's Farmland for Road Construction: Yu Mingxin, the director of the Jiangdu Construction Bureau, reported that the Jiang Gua-Yu Road construction started on the 12th. Apart from Zhu Gongxi, the technical section chief, who remained in the bureau to supervise the project, the engineering and technical supervisors were dispatched to Junbo to set up a road construction sub-team office to supervise the northern section of the road. On the 14th, while Yu and Xu, the leader of the road team, were convening a meeting in Junbo with the heads of the seventh and eighth districts to discuss effective measures, over 300 women suddenly rushed in, holding horse brushes, dirty cloths, and other foul items. They claimed they were petitioning the director to preserve the farmland used for the road construction to maintain their livelihoods, otherwise they would resort to desperate measures. Armed police arrived and, through strenuous explanation, managed to disperse the unconscious women's group. Yu returned to Yangzhou on the morning of the 16th to report to the county magistrate and then traveled by car across the river to report the situation to the construction minister, requesting instructions.

Liang Guanying Enlists Bandits: Liang Guanying, the commander of the 25th Route, has been stationed in Jiangbei and has suppressed many large gangs of local bandits in the Huaiyang counties, rescuing many hostages. Many of the remaining bandits have fled into the Lixia River area. A group of three to four hundred bandits sent a letter requesting Commander Liang's permission to surrender with their weapons. Their request was approved, and they were instructed to gather in Sisui Town, under the jurisdiction of Chu Ying County, to await enlistment. Currently, over two hundred remaining bandits have gathered in Sisui and are being monitored by the local garrison. Once the number is complete, Commander Liang will report to Pacification Commissioner Zhang and dispatch personnel to verify and reorganize them.

Gaoyou 86

Compilation of Robbery Cases: On the night before last, around 11 PM, more than 20 bandits speaking with a northern accent suddenly arrived at Situ Tan Town in the county. Armed with Mauser pistols, they robbed door-to-door until about 4 AM the next morning, before carrying away the stolen goods and escaping north on their original boat. It is said that the seven stores, including Chou Changsheng's, suffered the greatest losses. They have reported the case to the city government, requesting a strict investigation. Also, at the home of farmer Lu Changyi in Jiujin Xia Village, over 10 bandits suddenly arrived the day before yesterday. Armed with firearms, they broke down the door, first tying up Lu's wife, Zheng, and then rushing into the bedroom to search thoroughly. It is said that they lost about a hundred yuan.

Nantong 87

Military Police Seize Sixteen Bags of Opium: At 6 AM on the 16th, the Taikoo Company's Wuchang steamer arrived at Nantong Yaogang and unloaded sixteen sacks of opium. The military police joint river patrol team seized the sacks. The opium smugglers had already escaped. The opium has been transported to the city. The two districts of Tongyang are accelerating the "cleansing the countryside" (清鄉) campaign. Zhao Jianxun, the Tongyang Pacification Commander, reported that while many bandits in the Huaiyang Tonghai districts have been eliminated, scattered bandits still harm the local population. He telegraphed the county magistrates, summoning them to a "cleansing the countryside" meeting. Police and militia teams from each district will gather once a week to patrol villages and towns, conducting a household survey to eliminate the source of bandits. Each county is rapidly implementing these measures.

Jiaxing 88

Captured Bandits Sent to Court: On the day before yesterday, detectives from the Jiaxing Second District River Police Department captured two bandits, Zhou Jinyou and Wan A’fu, in the Gao area of the East Gate. They were immediately brought back to the district headquarters for interrogation, where they confessed to multiple robbery cases. Yesterday, the River Police Department sent the two bandits to the local branch court for legal punishment. Also, on the day before yesterday, the County Public Security Bureau's detective team captured several bandits near the Mahal Tang Bridge in the county: Ye Ziming, Wang Deyi, Zhang Wu, Wang Ada, Wang Azhen, Li Asi, Hu Chunquan, and Li Wenying. After interrogation, they confessed to robberies in the Dumen Zhang family and the Chen family at the Mahal Tang Bridge. Yesterday, these bandits were also sent to court for trial with supporting documents.

A Large Group of Linhai Bandits Sent to Haiyan Prison for Trial: The Linhai bandits, Ren Daojiao, Huang Xiaohua, Lin Huayong, Li Yumei, Jin Ren, Pan Laogu, Wang Daocheng, Zheng Chonglai, Lin Benwen, Ye Yongzhi, Dao Wu, and Jin Liangsen, who committed serious kidnappings in the Haiyan County area of Jiaxing, fled back to their original hometowns in Linhai County. The Linhai County authorities successively arrested them and they confessed to crimes committed in Haiyan County. Therefore, the Linhai County government escorted these twelve criminals to the Haiyan County government for investigation and trial.

Huzhou 89

Kidnapping Case Occurs in Shuangdu Village: In Shuangdu Village in the southwestern countryside of the city, where most of the fifty-some families are named Chen, more than ten bandits suddenly arrived around 7 PM yesterday. Each was armed with firearms and carried electric torches. They broke into Chen's house. Four bandits guarded the front and back doors, while the remaining bandits entered and kidnapped the nearly sixty-year-old Chen. The bandits then robbed the Jiang family. Before leaving, they kidnapped Meng, a relative of the Jiang family.

Peace Night Boat Robbed: Yesterday afternoon, around 4 PM, the Peace Night Boat set off from the city. While passing through the Yangjia area, two bandits suddenly appeared, each holding a handgun, and forced the boat to dock. They jumped onto the boat and searched all the silver and cash hidden by the passengers, leaving nothing behind. The total loss is estimated to be over a hundred yuan.

Hangzhou 90

Ancient Corpse from the Ming Dynasty Discovered in Haiyan: An ancient tomb was discovered outside the West Gate of Haiyan the day before yesterday. After the grave robbers Feng Laifu and Pan Heshang were arrested for digging up bricks, splitting the coffin, and stealing artifacts, the county authorities discovered a white jade hairpin and four agate buttons. After sending the items to the county, they found a burial urn and a Ming Dynasty "road pass" (路引) from inside the coffin. The text on the vellum woodblock print was clear, filling in ten places with the Heavenly Prefecture seal in bright ink. The pass stated that the deceased was Zheng Cunren, a 25-year-old student of the Imperial Academy from Haiyan County, Jiaxing Prefecture, Zhejiang Province. County Magistrate Ruan consulted the county records and determined that Zheng was an imperial inspector from the Ming Dynasty, living about 400 years ago. He personally led his staff and local gentry to inspect the site. The corpse's torso was tall and slender, with black hair and grayish-white skin and flesh, remaining relatively intact. However, it had been dug into two pieces, and the ribs were black. The coffin and clothes were destroyed. The magistrate immediately purchased new clothing, hats, and a coffin for reburial and summoned the Star Photography Studio to take a photo for distribution for research.

Freight Railway to be Built Along the Beijing-Hangzhou Canal: Although the foundation of the Beijing-Hangzhou Highway has been laid for some time, the surface has not yet been paved. Recently, the Engineering Office has been actively paving the surface. In addition to transporting a large number of yellow stones for paving, more than ten ships of light rail tracks have been transported to set up the railway in the center of the road for freight transport. Construction is expected to begin soon.

Implementation of Inspection of Rice and Grain Exports: Zhejiang Province borders the sea and has a large population. The transport of rice and grain within the province has always been for relieving famine in neighboring areas and has not been prohibited. However, there is concern that unscrupulous merchants may use this as a pretext to transport and sell goods to the mainland, secretly smuggling them overseas for profit. A Maritime Prohibition Bureau (海禁局) was established in the past but was abolished due to poor management. Now, the authorities, to prioritize the people's food supply and strictly prohibit smuggling, have ordered customs officials to assist in strict inspections. A rice and grain export inspection office has been established at Haimen to implement inspections.

Educational News Highlights

Ministry of Education Announces Reproduction of the San Min Zhu Yi Thousand Character Primer 91

The Ministry of Education, following a central government resolution, has reproduced the San Min Zhu Yi (Three Principles of the People) Thousand Character Primer. The printing is now complete. Yesterday, the ministry issued a decree announcing nine measures for reproducing the San Min Zhu Yi Thousand Character Primer to facilitate printing and distribution by various bookstores. The measures are as follows: (1) Bookstores that publish educational materials may reproduce the officially printed San Min Zhu Yi Thousand Character Primer pledge edition, but must comply with these measures. (2) Bookstores wishing to reproduce the primer must submit an application along with two copies of the sample to the Ministry of Education for approval before distribution. (3) The application must include the following information: (a) the number of copies to be printed in each edition; (b) the intended use of the reproduced edition; (c) the price; (d) a declaration of the reproducing organization; (e) the name, address, and brief history of the distributor. (4) The text, format, and content of the reproduced edition must strictly adhere to the original and must not be added to, deleted from, or altered. The paper and cover must also be the same as the original, but the use of Chinese paper is preferred. (5) The reproduced edition must state "Issued with the approval of the Ministry of Education" on the upper left corner of the cover and may state "Printed by [Bookstore Name]" in the lower left corner. The full text of the Ministry of Education's approval for reproduction must be printed on the back cover. (6) In addition to the title and the items listed in the preceding article, no other words may be printed on the cover of the reproduced edition. The cover page must not contain advertisements or other printed text. (7) The selling price of the reproduced book must be approved by the Ministry of Education. (8) Those who reproduce the primer privately without complying with these measures will be prohibited from distributing it after investigation by the county government and reporting to higher authorities, who will then report it to the Ministry of Education. (9) These measures will take effect on the date of promulgation.

Central University Reorganizes School Affairs 92

Nanjing, 17th (Central News Agency): Central University announced on the 17th that it would strictly enforce attendance checks, change the curriculum, and relocate classrooms. The deadline is the 20th.

Ministry of Education Orders Beijing Municipal Government to Pay Close Attention to Educational Administration 93

The Beijing Municipal Government submitted its administrative plan for January to March of the 20th year to the Executive Yuan for review. The Executive Yuan ordered the Ministry of Education to conduct a detailed review of the plan within its jurisdiction and submit a report to the Yuan for review. After receiving the order, the Ministry of Education found that the plan failed to adequately consider the needs of official affairs in relation to schools and education. Yesterday, it issued a response to the Executive Yuan, requesting that the Beijing Municipal Government be ordered to pay close attention to educational administration and that the Municipal Education Bureau be ordered to quickly formulate a plan to promote and expand primary education in the capital, as well as a report on past progress, for submission to the Ministry for review.

The original response stated: "After reviewing this plan, it is found that the social education aspects are generally acceptable. However, the plan to add classes in the second semester for school education is insufficient to meet actual needs. It is proposed that the Executive Yuan order the Nanjing Municipal Government to pay close attention to educational administration and designate a certain percentage of the subsidies allocated by the Executive Yuan specifically for the promotion and expansion of primary education. It is also requested that the Executive Yuan order the Nanjing Municipal Education Bureau to quickly submit a special report to the Ministry on the plan to promote and expand primary education and the progress made in the past two and a half months for review and decision."

Jiangsu Department of Education Orders County Education Bureaus to Report on the Use of Salt Tax Surcharges for Educational Expenses 94

In order to facilitate the transfer and allocation of funds.

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education Order No. 505 instructs the county education bureaus to fill out and submit forms to the department regarding the Yangzhou Audit Sub-Bureau's letter on the collection of educational fees from the salt tax surcharges on the Huainan coastal salt and the four banks of the Yangtze River, which are collected by the sub-bureau, so that the funds can be transferred and allocated.

The Yangzhou Audit Sub-Bureau's official letter stated that it was based on General Audit Office Order No. 201, which was based on Ministry of Finance Instruction No. 24952, which was based on Executive Yuan Instruction, which was based on National Government Order No. 703. The order stated that salt tax is a national revenue and local governments should not levy surcharges. However, due to the turbulent situation, provinces have often relied on salt tax surcharges to easily obtain substantial funds, disregarding the principle of taxation and cleverly establishing names to heavily burden the people. Although a clear order was issued last year to recover and reorganize the surcharges, a small number of provinces have failed to comply because the funds were specifically designated for specific purposes and it was difficult to compensate for the previous deficits. Now that the military situation has stabilized and the national government follows proper procedures, the salt tax is crucial to the central government's finances, and the fragmentation and division that hinders unification cannot be tolerated. Therefore, the Audit Yuan is ordered to instruct all provinces to comply with the order that all existing salt tax surcharge provinces must uniformly transfer the surcharges to the Ministry of Finance for unified collection and review for separate reductions and overall reorganization by March 1, 1931. Even if the surcharge was originally designated for a specific purpose and it is difficult to make up for it in the short term, the province should truthfully report it to the Yuan for review, and the Yuan should instruct the Ministry of Finance to find a way to make appropriate allocations to provide relief and should not delay on the pretext of resistance. After this transfer to the central government for collection and reorganization, local areas must not establish any other names to levy salt tax surcharges, lest they be investigated. This order, etc., in addition to being distributed to the provincial and municipal governments for compliance, is also sent to the various salt affairs agencies for detailed investigation and reporting. The head office is also ordered to instruct the auditing agencies in the various salt districts to quickly and thoroughly investigate the names, tax rates, reasons for levying, time limits, and actual uses of the various surcharges in each district, and to propose appropriate arrangements for the takeover and future reorganization, and report them to the head office within ten days of receiving this document for review and forwarding. This matter is of utmost importance, and no delay is permitted. The sub-bureau is ordered to comply with the ministry's order to investigate, report, and propose arrangements within the time limit to facilitate review and forwarding. This matter concerns educational expenses, and no delay is permitted. According to this, the sub-bureau shall comply with the order. The investigation revealed that merchants in the Huainan coastal salt area pay 5 cents per salt catty for educational expenses, and merchants transporting salt on the four banks pay 9 li per salt picul for educational expenses. These funds are drawn and transported by the salt merchants' associations to the educational institutions for collection and verification. It is reported that the former donations are allocated for use by 21 counties, including Jiangning and Jiangdu. The collection of these funds in the form of surcharges should be transferred to this sub-bureau for collection and credited to the Ministry of Finance from March 1. If the educational institutions in the counties have a need for these funds, they can request the provincial government to transfer them to the Ministry of Finance for allocation. In view of the foregoing, you are hereby requested to investigate and instruct the education bureaus of the counties that allocate these funds. It has been found that this province uses salt tax surcharges to fund education expenses. However, if the county's education expenses have this surcharge, it should quickly investigate to facilitate the transfer and allocation. In addition to issuing separate orders to the Jiangdong bureaus, you are also ordered to investigate and submit the forms to the Nuclear Bureau within three days of receiving this document for review and processing. This matter concerns educational expenses, and no delay is permitted.

Tsinghua Student Representatives Host Beijing Reporters 95

Tsinghua University student representatives Lin Wenqian, Liu Hanwen, and Wang Zhen arrived in Beijing and hosted fourteen reporters from various news outlets at the Central Hotel at 6 PM on the 14th. Liu Hanwen first reported that since Luo Jialun's resignation, the university has been maintained by the university affairs meeting. This meeting is currently being led by the acting provost and the deans of the three faculties (arts, science, and law). They are not fully responsible and each person has their own job responsibilities and are unable to oversee everything. Therefore, they are only going through the motions and their measures are unsatisfactory. Ten months have passed and the situation cannot continue. The president of the university has repeatedly cabled to the Ministry of Education, firmly resigning. Also, Tsinghua has a beautiful environment, sufficient funds, and complete facilities. If a president can be found to lead the entire university and the faculty and students cooperate and work hard to develop it, it will not be difficult to become an ideal and perfect higher education institution in the future. Therefore, the appointment of a new president is the unanimous and urgent request of the entire university. However, not having a president is better than having an incompetent president. Having a president who is not suitable is even worse than not having one. Therefore, the students of the university believe that the successor should have at least the following qualifications: rich experience in running schools, well-known reputation, noble character, and profound scholarship. At the same time, they must be able to focus on education, do education for the sake of education, and have the determination and plans to develop Jihua. Based on the above, they hope that the government can select one from the three gentlemen: Zhou Yichun, Zhao Yuanren, and Hu Shi. However, if there is someone more suitable than these three, they will not reject them. The representatives met with Sun Benwen, the director of the Department of Higher Education of the Ministry of Education, on the 13th, and with Chen Bulei, the vice minister, on the 14th. They have registered to request an audience with Chairman Chiang. In their presentation to the Ministry of Education, Chen and Sun did not give any specific indication. However, they said that the national government has approved Luo Jialun's resignation and has internally decided on a successor. However, the successor cannot be announced because the national government meeting has not yet approved it. The representatives repeatedly requested information so that they could relay it to the students, but they were all refused. The reason why the government has been extremely conservative and secretive about the selection of the next president of Tsinghua is that many people are vying for the position. They fear that announcing it officially will cause opposition and disputes from various parties. The representatives finally expressed their hope that the government would carefully select the successor to avoid repeating the same mistake. Chen also said that he would take it into consideration. Subsequently, Wang reported on the brief history of the university and the current situation. Then, a reporter spoke. The hosts and guests parted happily around 8 PM.

Declaration of the Eighth Representative Assembly 98

The future of Jiangsu education is alarming. Since the sixteenth year of the Republic [1927], educational funding has largely relied on land tax appropriations, and the overdue payments from various counties have exceeded two million yuan. In the past two years, the province's educational funding revenues and expenditures have accumulated a deficit of over one million yuan. At this time of year, when harvests are abundant and tax collection is at its peak, the accumulated arrears of various schools still exceed two months. School principals are running around and appealing, but to no avail, and the Education Funding Committee is also sighing helplessly, unable to find a solution. The principles of the late Premier Sun Yat-sen on ensuring educational funding and Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's orders on rectifying academic atmosphere and increasing funding are clearly being contradicted. Who should be held accountable for the ineffective fundraising? We colleagues are employed here and initially had no responsibility for planning funding, nor did we disapprove of the authorities' measures. However, since we regard education as our profession, we should treat education as our life. The prolonged delay in funding will break the vitality of schools, and the relationship between spirit and matter is particularly close. If funding is sufficient and arrangements are thorough, the academic atmosphere will naturally improve; otherwise, even if we strive to rectify it, it will be as difficult as rowing against the current. We colleagues are committed to schools and love them as our homes. Therefore, for many years, we have been diligently teaching, showing loyalty and dedication, and never daring to neglect our duties due to financial constraints. Moreover, how can we bear to see the discipline of schools decline due to financial constraints? This sincere heart is why we endure the pain temporarily, hoping for a better future. Who knew that year after year, things would get worse and worse? A good harvest leads to wives weeping, and a warm year leads to children crying from the cold. Personal lives are difficult to maintain, and the education system is gradually declining. Rather than forgetting the precept of not exceeding our position, how can we forget the duty that every citizen has? Jiangsu education is at a point of exhaustion. Knowing its danger and not shouting loudly to support it is disloyal, not loosening our hair and fastening our coronets to save it is unjust, and not adding fuel to the fire to preserve it is unwise. We colleagues, driven by our conscience, have no choice but to make a corresponding expression, so as to urge the authorities to awaken, which still stems from our love for the school, not only to maintain our livelihoods. Moreover, the material treatment we colleagues receive is already so meager. How about the spiritual comfort we get? The director of the Education Department sits high in the hall, unaware of what education is. When difficulties arise, he does not think of ways to solve them. When problems occur, he only knows how to deal with them with high-pressure tactics. We colleagues are suffering and moaning, unable to find comfort for ourselves. If we are blocked from reporting upwards and want to gather opinions to make suggestions, we are suspected of causing trouble and are subjected to coercion and bribery. This is their specialty. Because of this, we have fulfilled our duty for two years. Strong and capable people have been dismissed one after another, and the spirit of hard-boned loyalty has become sycophantic. The spirit of education has been swept away from this point. This is why we colleagues are fearful of the future and have no choice but to weep and tell those who care about education. We hereby submit the following urgent issues for immediate relief for the government and society to investigate:

1. Request the education authorities to recover the educational funding overdue from various counties.

2. Request the education authorities to follow the late Premier Sun Yat-sen's instructions to ensure the independence of Jiangsu's educational funding and cease allocating funds to the National Central University.

3. Request the education authorities to find new sources of government funding and allocate a percentage from the provincial business tax to supplement educational funding.

4. The funding for each school this semester is nearly three months in arrears. Request the education authorities to quickly issue the funds to maintain the status quo.

5. The cost of living has continued to rise, and the compensation for teachers and staff is still based on the standards stipulated in the sixteenth year of the Republic [1927], which is one-fifth lower than that of neighboring provinces. Request the education authorities to find ways to increase compensation to maintain livelihoods.

6. Regarding educational facilities, the administrative authorities should gather broad opinions and adopt them with the situation, and should not arbitrarily refuse based on personal opinions. March 18, 1931.

Regulations on the Number of Participants from Lower-Level Education Associations in Higher-Level Education Associations 99

The Shanghai County Education Bureau received Instruction No. 472 from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education yesterday, stating: "1. Following instructions: Regarding the Ministry of Education's telegraphed inquiry on the number of representatives to be elected by the members' general assembly of lower-level education associations to attend the members' general assembly of higher-level education associations, the number of representatives should be two from the district education association and one from the county or city education association. The term of office is tentatively set at one year. In addition to the elected representatives from the lower-level education associations, other members of the county and city education associations, provincial education association directors and supervisors, and other officers also have the right to be elected. Apart from distributing this to the lower levels, you are hereby instructed to be informed and comply." On the same day, a telegram was also received from the Ministry of Education stating that when lower-level education associations are required to attend meetings of higher-level education associations, they should elect representatives to attend the meeting. The number of representatives should be in accordance with Article 5 of the Party Department's Guidance on the Reorganization and Organization of Education Associations, with two representatives from the district education association and one from the county or city education association. The term of office for representatives is tentatively set at one year. You are hereby instructed to be informed and comply. You are also instructed to inform and ensure compliance among your subordinates. Thus, this instruction is hereby issued for your information and to instruct your subordinates to be informed and comply accordingly."

Minutes of the Shanghai County Education Bureau's Bureau Affairs Meeting 100

After holding the memorial week on the morning of the day before yesterday, the Shanghai County Education Bureau held its 192nd bureau affairs meeting. (3) Committee Member Niu reported that Hua Jing Elementary School requested to add a grade. It was resolved that due to lack of funding, it was difficult to approve. (4) Committee Member Niu reported that Cangqiao Elementary School requested to hire an additional assistant teacher. (5) Committee Member Niu reported that Dongming Elementary School requested to reduce the budget for tuition fees for the 20th year of the Republic [1931]. It was resolved that most of the school's tuition fees were used to repay the construction costs of the school building, and the request was difficult to approve for the time being. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.
